Emphasize particularly the marks used to identify the bird, but include a complete description of the bird.  Include size, overall shape, plumage and color pattern; details on shape or size of bill, wings, and tail.  Describe what you are actually observing in the field.----A duck, virtually identical in size and structure to nearby American Wigeons.  Pale gray flanks and on back fading to slightly brownish on wing tips.  Pale pinkish/rose-colored on breast.  White on abdomen and a band above the base of the tail.  The tail was black.  The head and neck were bright maroon-rufous with a buffy-white disk on the forehead.  The bird had white horizontal bars along the flanks about 1/3 of the way down the body.  ----Describe the bird's overall behavior:--The bird was closely associating with a flock of American Wigeons.  Foraging actively in sahllow water and at times resting on a mud flat.  A few times I noted aggressive encounters with other male wigeons. ----Describe the habitat in which you observed the bird:--Medium sized man-made reservoir.  The flock was sticking close to the edge of the reservoir lined partially with cattail marsh and partially with an alkaline mud flat.  Surrounding matrix of of saltbush desert scrub, sedge meadows, and young ash groves.----Describe the bird's calls or sounds, if heard, including method of delivery, i.e., from perch, in flight, etc.:  Did not vocalize during any of my observations.----List similar species and how you eliminated them:  Easily separated from American Wigeon by rufous head and neck, buffy-white forehead disk, uniform gray flanks, lack of green on head.  The bird was closely examined for features consistent with American Wigeon and none were detected, eliminating the possibility of a hybrid.--Prior experience with this and similar species:  I have seen this species in several consecutive winters in Albuquerque NM, often at close range, once in Scottsdale AZ, and once at Bolinas Lagoon in northern California.----Optical equipment:--Viewed through Nikon Prostaff 20-60X82 Spotting Scope.----If photographed, please enclose a copy or attach digital copy to email.  --Photo equipment used:  Digiscoped using above mentioned spotting scope and a rather cheap Olympus digital camera.----Other observers who independently identified the bird (please list name and address if known):--None----Additional discussion:----References consulted:--None needed.----This report was written from notes made during _X_ after ___ observation (from memory).--If "after, from memory", approximately how long after the observation were notes first written:------Name: Carl G.
